## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillations (velocity-space oscillator modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is an acceleration and the available state variable is v (velocity) with time t, which matches reduced-form or velocity-only models of nonlinear oscillators where acceleration depends on damping/forcing terms that are functions of v and/or periodic functions of t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Constant acceleration (bias/drift): dv_dt = c0 (sensor bias, constant external acceleration)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (local linearization of drag/damping; c0 typically negative)
- Time-dependent damping: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * v (slowly varying dissipation or effective gain)
- Quadratic drag (speed-dependent): dv_dt = c0 * v * Abs(v) (turbulent/pressure drag-like dissipation)
- Cubic nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v**3 (high-velocity nonlinear dissipation)
- Mixed linear+cubic (Rayleigh-type) damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (captures negative damping at small |v| and saturation at larger |v| depending on signs)
- Dry/Coulomb friction (idealized): dv_dt = c0 * sign(v) (velocity-opposing friction; discontinuous at v=0)
- Smooth Coulomb friction approximation: dv_dt = c0 * tanh(c1 * v) (regularized sign(v) for numerical/physical smoothing)
- Sinusoidal external forcing: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) (periodic drive producing oscillatory acceleration)
- Multi-harmonic forcing: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (drive with harmonics/sidebands)
- Forcing plus damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (driven damped oscillator in velocity form)
- Parametrically modulated damping/drive: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (time-periodic modulation producing parametric resonance-like effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Dissipation proportional to velocity → dv_dt contains a term c*v with c<0 (exponential decay of v in absence of forcing).
- Aerodynamic/turbulent drag → dv_dt includes v*Abs(v) (odd in v, stronger damping at higher speeds).
- Nonlinear saturation of damping or self-excitation → combination c0*v + c1*v**3 (small-amplitude growth if c0>0 with amplitude limiting if c1<0).
- Dry friction/stiction → sign(v) behavior; use tanh(c*v) to model smoothing near v=0 and avoid discontinuities.
- Periodic external drive → sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms; phase/amplitude determine steady-state response.
- Beating or complex drive spectra → sums of multiple sinusoids with different frequencies (multiple peaks in dv_dt vs t).
- Parametric effects → coefficients multiplying v vary periodically, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*v (can create instability tongues/resonance).
- Odd symmetry in v for velocity-dependent forces → dv_dt terms are often odd functions of v (v, v^3, v*Abs(v), tanh(c*v)), consistent with force reversing when velocity reverses.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: -0.0834*v³ - 0.9954*log(|v| + 1) + 0.7824*sin(t)**

The key components are:
1. A **sin(t)** term (or equivalently cos(t + phase shift))
2. A **v³** term
3. A **log(|v| + 1)** term

The critical question for each candidate is whether its basis functions can reproduce **log(|v| + 1)**. This is the hardest term to match since log is transcendental and cannot be exactly represented by polynomials, exponentials, rational functions, or other non-log basis functions.

Let me systematically check which candidates contain a **log** term that could match log(|v| + 1):

- **Candidates with log terms**: 7, 15, 21, 50
- **Candidates with Abs(v)/(c + Abs(v))**: 1, 2, 6, 8, 13, 14, 16, 18, 19, 23, 28, 37, 38, 40, 41, 42, 43, 44, 45, 46, 48 — These are rational functions, NOT equivalent to log.
- **Candidates with exp terms but no log**: Many — exp cannot reproduce log.
- **Candidates with only polynomial/trig/exp/abs terms**: Cannot match log(|v|+1).

Let me check the log-containing candidates:

**Candidate 7**: `c0 + c1*sin(c2*v + c3) + c4*log(c5*v + 1) + c6*cos(c7 + t) + c8*Abs(v) + c9*v³ + v`

The log term is log(c5*v + 1), not log(|v| + 1). Since v takes both signs, log(c5*v + 1) is NOT the same as log(|v| + 1). For v < 0, |v| = -v, so we'd need log(-c5*v + 1) simultaneously, which is impossible with a single log(c5*v + 1). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 15**: `c0*v + c1 + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*log(c6*v + 1) + c7*cos(c8 + t) + c9*Abs(v)`

Same issue — log(c6*v + 1) ≠ log(|v| + 1) for both signs of v. Also missing v³. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 21**: `c0 + c1*sin(c2*v + c3) + c4*log(c5*v + 1) + c6*cos(c7 + t) + c8*Abs(v) + c9*v + v`

Same log issue, no v³. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 50**: `c0 + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*Abs(v) + c4*v³ + c5*Abs(v)/(c6 + Abs(v)) + c7*exp(c8*v)*log(c9*|v| + 1)`

Has log(c9*|v| + 1) but multiplied by exp(c8*v). Setting c8=0 gives c7*log(c9*|v|+1). With c9=1, this gives log(|v|+1). Then we need c5*|v|/(c6+|v|) to vanish (set c5=0), and c3*|v| to vanish (set c3=0). We'd have: c0 + c1*cos(c2+t) + c4*v³ + c7*log(|v|+1). Setting c2 = -π/2 gives sin(t). This matches! **MATCH.**

Let me verify Candidate 50: c0=0, c1=0.7824, c2=-π/2, c3=0, c4=-0.0834, c5=0, c7=-0.9954, c8=0, c9=1. ✓
